# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Upstream Connection Pool Overflow

## Your Task

Envoy logs show 'upstream connection pool overflow' errors during traffic spikes. Find the C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that (1) define the overflow state in the connection pool and (2) emit or handle this overflow condition.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)

- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Envoy codebase and created a comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

I identified the C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that define and handle the 'upstream connection pool overflow' condition:

### Core Files:
1. **envoy/common/conn_pool.h** - Defines the `PoolFailureReason` enum with the `Overflow` state
2. **source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc** - Implements overflow detection and handling in:
   - `attachStreamToClient()` (max streams overflow)
   - `newStreamImpl()` (max pending streams and load shedding overflow)
3. **source/common/upstream/conn_pool_map_impl.h** - Increments `upstream_cx_pool_overflow_` counter when connection pool creation fails

### Statistics and Counters:
- **envoy/upstream/upstream.h** - Defines the overflow counters in the stats macros:
  - `upstream_cx_pool_overflow` (connection pool circuit breaker overflow)
  - `upstream_rq_pending_overflow` (pending requests overflow)
  - `upstream_cx_overflow` (connection circuit breaker overflow)

### Protocol-Specific Implementations:
- **source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h/cc** - HTTP connection pool implementation
- **source/common/tcp/conn_pool.cc** - TCP connection pool implementation
- **source/common/tcp_proxy/tcp_proxy.cc** - TCP proxy overflow handling
- **source/extensions/filters/udp/udp_proxy/udp_proxy_filter.cc** - UDP proxy overflow handling

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains detailed information about files, symbols, the call chain, and a comprehensive narrative explanation of how the overflow condition is defined and propagated through Envoy's connection pool system.

This increments the `upstream_rq_pending_overflow_` counter.\\n\\n2. **Max Pending Streams Overflow** (lines 347-353 in `newStreamImpl`): When the number of pending requests reaches the maximum allowed by the cluster resource manager, the code logs \\\"max pending streams overflow\\\" and triggers a pool failure with overflow reason, incrementing `upstream_rq_pending_overflow_`.\\n\\n3. **Load Shedding Overflow** (lines 379-384 in `newStreamImpl`): When the connection pool cannot create a connection due to load shedding (ConnectionResult::LoadShed), it cancels the pending stream and calls `onPoolFailure()` with overflow reason.\\n\\n### Connection Pool Resource Limits\\nIn **source/common/upstream/conn_pool_map_impl.h** (lines 35-39), the `getPool()` method manages connection pool resource limits. When attempting to create a new connection pool, if the resource limit (`connectionPools()` circuit breaker) cannot be created, the code attempts to free an idle pool. If no idle pool can be freed and the limit is reached, it increments the `upstream_cx_pool_overflow_` counter and returns an error.\\n\\n### Counter Definitions\\nThe counters tracking overflow are defined in **envoy/upstream/upstream.h** (line 726):\\n- `upstream_cx_pool_overflow`: Total times the cluster's connection pool circuit breaker overflowed\\n- `upstream_rq_pending_overflow`: Total times pending requests exceeded the configured limit\\n- `upstream_cx_overflow`: Total connection circuit breaker overflows (separate from pool overflow)\\n\\n### HTTP and TCP Implementation\\n**source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h** (lines 85-91) and **source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc** provide the HTTP-specific implementation of `onPoolFailure()`, which extracts the callback from the HTTP attach context and invokes it with the pool failure reason.\\n\\n**source/common/tcp/conn_pool.cc** provides the TCP implementation of the connection pool, inheriting the overflow handling from the base class.\\n\\n### Proxy Filters\\nBoth TCP and UDP proxies explicitly handle overflow conditions:\\n- **source/common/tcp_proxy/tcp_proxy.cc** (line 686): Increments `upstream_cx_overflow_` when a TCP connection cannot be established due to resource constraints.\\n- **source/extensions/filters/udp/udp_proxy/udp_proxy_filter.cc** (lines 823, 1044): Increments `upstream_cx_overflow_` when UDP sessions hit the session circuit breaker.\\n\\n### Summary\\nThe upstream connection pool overflow is a sophisticated resource management mechanism that prevents exhaustion of connection resources. The overflow state is defined centrally in `PoolFailureReason`, triggered through multiple resource limit checks in `ConnPoolImplBase::newStreamImpl()` and `ConnPoolImplBase::attachStreamToClient()`, and tracked through counters in the cluster traffic statistics.
